    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer11360057375409108963">Mackenzie "Mac" Nighthorse is a highly respected homicide detective and a career cop. There isn't a dangerous situation that can back him down. However, the personal becomes uncomfortably entangled in the professional when he goes undercover in a high class BDSM club as a male submissive to find a Dominatrix who is winning the trust and then murdering her chosen partners. </span>
  <span id="freeText11360057375409108963" style="display:none">Mackenzie "Mac" Nighthorse is a highly respected homicide detective and a career cop. There isn't a dangerous situation that can back him down. However, the personal becomes uncomfortably entangled in the professional when he goes undercover in a high class BDSM club as a male submissive to find a Dominatrix who is winning the trust and then murdering her chosen partners. When his path crosses Violet Siemanski's, he realizes he's found a Mistress willing to be his ally in finding the murderess. But Violet is also going to shatter Mac's shields and make him question who he is and what he wants, a challenge more disturbing than any case he's ever worked.</span>

Mistress Violet is prowling <i>The Zone</i> when she sets her eyes on Mac and she knows right away that she wants him. She's very attracted to him, but Violet wants more than his body he so freely offers. Vi wants to understand his mind and she wants to crawl into his soul. Although Mac tries to fight her off, he has to cave in eventually. At the same time he has to face his fears. Their relationship is a bond of trust, and that trust should never be betrayed. Mac always felt D/s was about strength and power. But he's wrong because it's about trust and power exchange. Besides, it's about surrender for both of them and they must be open and honest about what they want and expect from each other.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382462132ra/5902023.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_mn7o03lZHx1rl28tmo1_500_zps661423df.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Mackenzie (Mac) Nighthorse is simply GORGEOUS! <br><br>Forty-three years old, 6 feet four inches tall, 220 pounds packed with muscles, broad shoulders, a body built like a football player's that emanates raw sexuality as all get out. His nickname is The Oak coz he's got a steadfast nature and works best under pressure. Straight nose, silver eyes, dark straight eyebrows, silky dark hair interwoven with white and silver. YUMMY! I love his name that seemed to be a pun (stud, Vi's play zone, equestrian sports), but his physique and character are absolutely stunning! Whew. He's a man's man, for sure. In fact, he's beyond sexy and totally mesmerizing. Mac combines all the mouth-wateringly hot attributes that I love to see in my heroes and to top everything off, he knows how to cook. Oh my, you should have seen him in his super tight jeans, topless, feet bare, standing in front of the counter chopping veggies. Sheesh, reel it in Baba. Mac DESERVES FIVE STARS ALONE.<br><br><blockquote>

    <i>"Take the wine." She lifted it. "And drink. Drink it all, until the last swallow, and then give me that last swallow from your mouth."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380399843ra/774197.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_mc85ml5MUX1rdd58ro1_500_zpsb4ad33b2.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>

    <blockquote>"Perhaps next time I have wine in my mouth," he murmured against her lips, "you'll let me put your legs on my shoulders, and I'll put my mouth on your pussy, slip my tongue in your c@nt and let all that warm, red wine run down inside. Mix with your sweet taste and drink from that."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>I remember when I read Natural Law for the very first time I couldn't believe that such a fabulous hunk--such an ALPHA--would submit to a little pixie. I had a hard time dealing with the fact that Mac enjoyed going on his knees for a Mistress and accepting whatever she dished out to him. After doing another reread I believe him. Mac wants a woman (in this case Vi) to dominate him in the bedroom; it's what he desires and needs to be happy. <br>Yet he feels it's a man's responsibility to protect a woman and keep her safe from harm. Violet is everything to Mac--Mistress, lover, friend, woman. It's humbling and exhilarating all at once but it also terrifies him. He doesn't want to be vulnerable in front of her. So, while Mac is all alpha on the job and in other aspects of his life, it gives him great pleasure to submit to Vi's bidding.<br><br>I must confess that I didn't like Vi when I read Natural Law for the first time, and even now I couldn't warm up to her. Mac didn't want it and yet she did it anyway. Funnily enough, I really liked her in Tyler and Marguerite's story <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/177518.Ice_Queen__Nature_of_Desire___3_" title="Ice Queen (Nature of Desire, #3) by Joey W. Hill" rel="nofollow noopener">Ice Queen</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1285705.Mirror_of_My_Soul__Nature_of_Desire___4_" title="Mirror of My Soul (Nature of Desire, #4) by Joey W. Hill" rel="nofollow noopener">Mirror of My Soul</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18239760.Tyler_Tied_Up__Nature_of_Desire__7_2_" title="Tyler Tied Up (Nature of Desire #7.2) by Joey W. Hill" rel="nofollow noopener">Tyler Tied Up</a>. It's odd because it's like swapping sides.   <span id="freeText14077098786281874066" style="display:none">I fucking hated this book. <br /><br />1. There are only two Black people in this book. Two. In Florida. Yeah. They're identical twins: Tamara and Keira. Guess who the crazy, psycho, sadistic, incestuous, damaged, murderous pair is in this book? Wild guess? Anyone?<br /><br />2. The purple prose is off the charts. Lay off the thesaurus, the allegories, and overly ornate everything. Every sexual experience is a volcano, a tsunami, an earthquake, a sunset, an astronomical wonder. Stop. Goddamn.<br /><br />3. Using "for" as a conjunction is pretentious and stupid. For example: He wanted a sandwich, for he was filled with a ravenous hunger. Versus: He wanted a sandwich because he was hungry...or since he was hungry. See how simple the last two are. Note how 'because' and 'since' don't give the reader pause and make them feel that they're reading something written in Middle English. Get off your pretentious horse, Hill. Your prose is ridiculous.<br /><br />4. The police everything in here is laughable. Bitch, watch some Law &amp; Order first at least. Please. How does a detective with 20 years on the force get made by everybody? And he makes no one, has no insight, and is too busy being led around by his magical dick to solve the case and find the murderers operating right under his nose. How does he enter dangerous situations with zero backup? How does his sergeant just let him do what he wants because 'he Alpha-man'? <br /><br />5. "I must break through the bounds of your mind, for you will surrender to me, your one and only, whereupon I shall own you heart, penis, and soul." You shall do this because I feel love after two scenes and there is no need to inform nor negotiate with the sub whose very being I shall claim and subsume into my own."<br />Where does "breaking" enter into D/s? Ignorant vanilla people need to stop writing about shit they don't know nor understand. <br /><br />7. Everyone's wealthy. Where's Cara McKenna's realistic writing when you need it? <br /><br />8. The soap opera drama that vacillates between being a Lifetime movie and a Schwarzenegger shoot-em-up film. Pop psychology aka BDSM shaming and police hero worship. Both utterly problematic, unentertaining, and revelatory of the fact that Hill needs to get some bloody perspective.<br /><br />9. Bitch can't write for shit.<br /><br />10. Failed, failed, failed femdom. <br />Thankfully, at least, it was a Lendle loan because I'd be calling Amazon for a return on this rubbish. <br /><br /><br /><b>TL:DR = Fuck this offensive piece of shit book written by a racist, no-talent hack. </b></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10963535238133452986"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“You’re mine, Mackenzie, and I don’t share you, not even with memories.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/>Once upon a time, I asked a trusted fellow reviewer which BDSM book she would recommend if she had to pick only one from the countless ones she has read so far, and this was her choice. Now, that’s all the convincing I needed to start reading this book immediately, but I was also dying of curiosity to see for myself what made this story so unique that a seasoned reader of the genre would single it out so adamantl</span>
  <span id="freeText10963535238133452986" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“You’re mine, Mackenzie, and I don’t share you, not even with memories.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>Once upon a time, I asked a trusted fellow reviewer which BDSM book she would recommend if she had to pick only one from the countless ones she has read so far, and this was her choice. Now, that’s all the convincing I needed to start reading this book immediately, but I was also dying of curiosity to see for myself what made this story so unique that a seasoned reader of the genre would single it out so adamantly. Well, let me tell you, I get it, I am now singling it out myself and would recommend it to anyone looking for an impressively written, intensely emotional and flaming-hot story that somehow manages to melt your heart and make you tingle to the tips of your toes all at the same time. It might be set within a BDSM framework, and the plotline relies heavily on this theme, but this book takes taboo to a whole new level of literary excellence. I am not ashamed to say that this was one of the most romantic books I have ever read and will forever remember it as that.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“I can take care of you, cherish you, and not consider you weak.”</i>
</blockquote><br>Unlike the vast majority of books in this genre, the dominant in this relationship is the female lead character and her counterpart is a somewhat unorthodox version of a male submissive – he is a policeman who dominates in all other aspects of his life, but enjoys handing over control in the bedroom, albeit preserving his powerful alpha tendencies.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“This man was big. Over six feet, the broadness in his shoulders was enough to accelerate her heart rate. He was pure male animal. No matter what soap, deodorant or cologne he used, he wouldn’t be able to obliterate the scent. He was powerful, a predator, but what made him absolutely irresistible to her, overriding her common sense, was that he was a sexual submissive. An alpha wolf who chose the role of beta in the bedroom, but only for the right woman.”</i>
</blockquote><br>When his latest murder case takes him into one of the most upscale and private BDSM clubs in the city, Mackenzie meets Violet, a young Domme with limited experience in the lifestyle, but a true dominant at the core of her sexual identity. He catches her eye immediately, his unmistakable submissive nature in stark contrast to his commanding alpha presence, and she is drawn to him like a moth to a flame.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“She wanted to tame the stallion that could not be tamed.”</i>
</blockquote><br>What starts as a cover for Mackenzie and an itch to be scratched for Violet, quickly escalates into something neither of them expected to find but their reaction to each other is off the charts. As Violet slowly strips him of his defensive armour, Mackenzie finally starts truly embracing his submissive proclivities, drawing pleasure, both physical as well as emotional, from exposing his vulnerabilities to his Mistress and surrendering all control. Violet is a skilled dominant, her emotional strength capable of bringing a man twice her size to his knees and obliterating his resolve. She methodically unlocks his guarded heart by bringing his body to its limits.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“You won’t use me or survive me, Mackenzie… When I’m done with you, you’ll belong to me. Heart, cock and soul.”</i>
</blockquote><br>This is a delicious and highly addictive tale of two people connecting on every possible level, and finding their natural place in a world that would judge them for their innate sexual tastes. Drawn to each other like two bright stars in the sky, they collide creating a supernova of emotions, but instead of just leaving shapeless remnants of who they used to be in the aftermath of that collision, they rebuild each other, they make each other stronger, and they “create a whole new universe” to be themselves in.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“You’re tearing me into pieces, sugar.”<br>“And I’ll know how to put them together,”</i>
</blockquote><br>This is one those perfect books – a perfect balance of plot, character development, sexual chemistry between the characters and flawless writing style. There’s a subtle philosophical undercurrent all throughout the storyline, a gentle critique of the D/s lifestyle and its drawbacks, and Ms Hill’s take on it is as inspiring as it is profound. This book owned me, body and soul, and it commanded every single heartbeat in my chest while I was reading it. I can envision myself re-reading it over and over again.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“… she’d found the fairy tale, someone who would share her life as well as her bed, someone who understood what she was, who she was. All the corners and rooms.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380382869i/740934.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="http://www.natashaisabookjunkie.com/2013/10/03/natural-law-joey-w-hill/" rel="nofollow noopener">See this review on my blog!</a> | <a href="http://www.facebook.com/natashaisabookjunkie" rel="nofollow noopener">Follow me on Facebook!</a> | <a href="http://www.twitter.com/natashabkjunkie" rel="nofollow noopener">Follow me on Twitter!</a></span>

Maybe it was curiosity or sheer boredom, but I finally gave in, and honestly wish I'd listened to my intuition. <u>Natural Law</u> wasn't epic fail as far as BDSM books go, but it was trying so hard to be so many things that it just didn't succeed at any of them. <br/><br/>I don't mind a bit of angst here and there, but every single character in this boo</span>
  <span id="freeText4001404502983130672" style="display:none">I'd put <u>Natural Law</u> off for several years in spite of all the glowing reviews, and it being that rare breed in BDSM fiction: a Fem-dom story (and I love those). Maybe it was curiosity or sheer boredom, but I finally gave in, and honestly wish I'd listened to my intuition. <u>Natural Law</u> wasn't epic fail as far as BDSM books go, but it was trying so hard to be so many things that it just didn't succeed at any of them. <br /><br />I don't mind a bit of angst here and there, but every single character in this book just needed to be put out of <i>my</i> misery. To be perfectly blunt (aren't I always), <u>Natural Law</u> came off as well, schizophrenic. On the one hand, Ms. Hill attempts to portray the BDSM lovestyle as just another form of sexual expression, and yet she inhabits her world with a bunch of people who were several cards short of a full deck. Thanks for the mixed message. Her club scenes left me rather nonplussed. I don't really don't know why every single BDSM club that gets written about is always high-end and filled with the creme de la creme of the beautiful people. Trust me, the scene is comprised of a mixed bag of looks and styles and it would be nice to read a BDSM-themed novel in which real people get to play (and enjoy themselves). Ms. Hill's bondage scenes were more about the tools and the toys. It was like browsing through the Extreme Restraints catalogue rather than the emotions and the trust issues involved, especially from Mac's point of view.<br /><br />Then for the shits and giggles there's a serial killer who preys upon sub men from said high-end BDSM club. Add to this a a twin-sister Domme act which was just squick city (and it takes quite a bit to squick me out) and well, it's just kind of a mess. Somewhere there's a romance, but it just seems to have been added because that's what readers expect. <br /><br />I actually had a lot of sympathy for Mac Nighthorse, and he really could have been a much richer and deeper character. It's very difficult within the confines of romancelandia to write about an alpha male hero who actually likes being dominated by a woman. Most women readers barely tolerate beta males in romance as it is. Now, us BDSM folks know and are used to such dynamics and few of us look askance or feel the need to challenge a man's masculinity. The way I've always seen it, it takes a very secure guy to allow himself to just let go and give up that instinct for control. In <u>Natural Law</u>, poor Mac is constantly explaining to himself, to outsiders and to the reader that while <i>"yes I'm a hunky cop/alpha male and I like to be whipped"</i>, he's still the one in control. He's still super-cop. I get it, really. In fact, practically every second or third page, Hill reminds us that Mac is "an alpha male". Honestly, he never really felt like a true sub, just a hunky guy with a kink. <br /><br />Nothing to say about Violet save FACE-PALM. Absolutely unbelievable as a top. She lacked any presence, and I'm not talking about her size (I'm a firm believer in what Jedi Master Yoda said about size, LOL). It was as if the author just had to make her shorter in order to yes, remind us that Mac is an...wait for it, wait for it...AN ALPHA MALE! Oh and sure, she too is in law enforcement, but guess what, she still ends up being rescued by Mac.<br /><br />I guess the sex scenes were hot. I seriously didn't notice them. That is pretty bad. The moral of this story? To listen to my intuition from now on. If I want well-written fem-dom, I'll just have to look elsewhere. Like Circlet Press.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14853176696505337937"><br/><b>**4.5 stars**</b><br/><br/>I LOVE the joy of discovering a new fantastic author! <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380395860ra/762653.gif' width='400' height='230' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Ok, maybe not new to most, but definitely new to me.<br/><br/>My stumble onto this book and author was purely accidental. Saw it was a freebie a few months ago, checked Amazon and GR for reviews, saw it rated rather highly and added it to the TBR and growing list of books awaiting me on my Kindle. <br/><br/>I’d been in a bit of a book slump going into this book and REALLY needed something to shake me up, so I thought, why not try a book about an Alp</span>
  <span id="freeText14853176696505337937" style="display:none"><br><b>**4.5 stars**</b><br><br>I LOVE the joy of discovering a new fantastic author! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380395860ra/762653.gif" width="400" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ok, maybe not new to most, but definitely new to me.<br><br>My stumble onto this book and author was purely accidental. Saw it was a freebie a few months ago, checked Amazon and GR for reviews, saw it rated rather highly and added it to the TBR and growing list of books awaiting me on my Kindle. <br><br>I’d been in a bit of a book slump going into this book and REALLY needed something to shake me up, so I thought, why not try a book about an Alpha male submissive?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380926359ra/3312273.gif" width="250" height="240" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I was a little weary of the subject matter (I like my men strong and I’d heard that Ms. Hill can write some intense BDSM), but I was going to power through and give it a chance. Boy am I glad I did‼ The first half of this book grabbed you by the balls and held on tight! Mac was ALL Alpha in his everyday life. Rugged homicide detective, hardcore muscle, pure testosterone…..but underneath that was a man who had primal sexual cravings, urgings to surrender control and the wicked desire to belong to someone. <br><br>His chemistry with Mistress Violet was electric and instant. Their first interaction was pretty intense, but by their second meeting……WOW. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381211496ra/4537049.gif" width="430" height="320" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>To say parts of this book made me feel uncomfortable would be an understatement…did Ms. Hill manage to make me feel uncomfortable yet hot and bothered at the same time…..UMMM HELL YES! Her writing is superb. Such finesse in showing what’s going on in a person’s mind and demonstrating how much deeper the connection is between two people in a BDSM lifestyle. More than just sexual gratification. That’s where her balance of the Alpha male submissive really came to light. Watching Violet break down Mac’s walls was really fascinating to see. <b>She didn’t make him weaker in any way, but only enhanced his authority. Authority to understand and accept his body’s needs, his mind’s thoughts, his heart’s desires and his soul’s cravings.</b><br><br>Now, after all that, unfortunately a couple of things kept this from being a blazing 5 star read (which I felt it could have been):<br><br>	1. Everything I’ve described above kind of loses its feel after about 75%-ish into the book. I understand what the author was going for and why everything unfolded the way it did, but it started confusing me a bit and I was wondering if the D/s balance was lost. For someone who understands the lifestyle more than I, this may be a bigger deal than I felt it was. I think I needed the intensity to simmer down a bit and just watch two people fall in love. But, nonetheless, I feel the need to point this out for those who might feel betrayed by the change.<br><br>	2. The last 10% felt a little off-kilter and not believable. Some of the revelations about the killer left me a bit stunned, speechless and frankly grossed out <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[UMMMMM she was her twin sister’s submissive?!?!?! WTF‼ <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I will say that I did not suspect who the killer ended up being, at all. I had my guesses, but I could not have guessed it would have gone in that direction and to that extent. And Mac’s ability to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[rip bolts and metal out of a floor using sheer force and rage….seriously, when did he turn into the Incredible Hulk? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. And my final head scratcher came in the form of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[a shoot out at the hospital, really? Even the explanation of how the twin sister was able to sneak in didn’t feel believable. And then Mac miraculously wakes up afterwards?? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. It felt like too much of a stretch for the sake of closure.<br><br><b>Overall, I highly recommend this book. Give it a go and see if it surprises you, like it did me! <br><br>Ms. Hill, you have made a fan out of me and I look forward to discovering more of your insightful creations one book at a time.</b><br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380419773ra/832596.gif" width="430" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/648282.gif" width="430" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

I like my men alpha and strong and loveable; and I found Mac to be the perfect blend, he was an alpha male outside the bedroom and would only submit to the one who could prove their worth on being his Mistress. In all the ways he submitted behind closed doors, I never found him to be weak, because like in all D/s relationships, the sub is the one who holds the power, regardless if they are bound, tied or gagged. Violet could very well hold her own, she was a woman who took her role as a Mistress seriously and wasn’t in it for just the fun, but the true connection between two people. <br><br>I kinda read this out of order, since this is book 2, but they are all standalone reads so it didn’t really matter. This may have referenced the characters from the first book, but gave nothing away that would spoil it for me. For me it was a great into to the series that I will now continue on without my previous hesitations.<br></span>

  <span id="freeText14813692197635161373" style="display:none">Someone is luring and killing men in the safety of their homes, in the intimacy of their bedrooms. Someone is winning trust and then betraying it in the worst way possible and to Mac Nighthorse, that is obscene. He knows the lifestyle and understands the Total Power Exchange between Mistress and Slave and for someone to betray that beautiful and freely given gift while in his city drives him into action. He risks his Sergeant's moral reaction when he tells her his plan to catch the woman known as the S&amp;M Killer, but he's willing to let himself out of the closet, so to speak. He's going to go undercover within the alluring club known as the Zone as a sexual submissive. His sergeant laughs, sure that someone of Mac's build and standing would never pass for a sub, but that's what he is. A sexually submissive male who craves the power of a Mistress's touch. Mistress Violet is prowling the Zone when she sees Mac. His powerful build and self assured masculinity screams out to her. As do the submissive wrist cuffs he wears. She wants him. She's attracted to him, but she wants more than the body he so freely offers her. She wants what no woman, no mistress has ever been able to touch. She wants his soul. She wants to tear open his body and crawl right in and once she has him by the balls, figuratively and literally, she's never letting go. <br /><br />Seriously, there are not enough words to express how much I love this book. I should say that the idea of femdom scares the bejesus out of me. I can't explain it but the idea of a woman breaking down a man just gives me the creeps. If I had a man strapped down to a rack, I wouldn't know what to do. But not Violet. She doesn't break Mac by just relentlessly lashing him, oh no. That would be too easy. She relentlessly breaks down all his emotional armor, past all the bullsh*it as she says and gets right to the man within, and it was seriously erotic as hell. Even though some of her methods had me squirming in discomfort, I was still absolutely one hundred percent fascinated. The relationship between Mac and Violet was so believable and so amazing that I closed this book with a sense of awe. <br /><br />Don't be like me, scared off by the idea of femdom. It's true that Violet holds the reins but Mac is no lightweight. He's no lap dog or doormat, and as he so charmingly tells her, he's nobody's pony. He's the pit bull who runs his own yard and he's delicious. He views his forays into BDSM almost as a workout. An exercise regiment. He normally looks at each Mistress with narrowed eyes and basically tells her, "do your worst, I can take it." He's like a soldier caught behind enemy lines, facing torture, who is screaming that no one will break him. Until Violet. <br /><br />Once Mac and Violet get past the power exchange their relationship really heats up. It was an incredible courtship and I adored it. Mac is just unbelievable. I am so in love with him. I don't care if he's a fictional character, I am in love. The level of their intimacy just blew me away and ye gods, I want that. You must read this book. Now.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81419817" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2909041430596049587">Natural Law, part of Joey Hill's Nature of Desire series, is probably one of the most realistic, well-written depictions of the more <i>extreme</i> side of BDSM that I have encountered. It's also the first "alpha male as sexual sub" or just "male-as-sub" erotic romance that I've read. I definitely prefer to read about males that stay alpha, in and out of the bedroom, but Joey Hill's writing captivated me anyway.<br/><br/>There's a Dom serial killer in town and respected homicide detective Mackenzie "Mac" Nightho</span>
  <span id="freeText2909041430596049587" style="display:none">Natural Law, part of Joey Hill's Nature of Desire series, is probably one of the most realistic, well-written depictions of the more <i>extreme</i> side of BDSM that I have encountered. It's also the first "alpha male as sexual sub" or just "male-as-sub" erotic romance that I've read. I definitely prefer to read about males that stay alpha, in and out of the bedroom, but Joey Hill's writing captivated me anyway.<br /><br />There's a Dom serial killer in town and respected homicide detective Mackenzie "Mac" Nighthorse suspects it's a female, a Mistress, behind the killings. It's always the same MO: each victim is late 20s, naked, bound, in a state of arousal, and with a bullet in the back of his head. Also, the killer likes to call the victim's family after each kill, so the victim's can be "outed" in death. The 1st two victims have one thing in common: they both frequented The Zone, a members only, exclusive, discreet and expensive fetish club in Tampa, FL. Unbeknownst to his colleagues, Mac, who has a quiet powerful presence when it comes to his job, has <i>actually</i> been on the fetish club scene for years as a sub. As people in the scene can spot true Doms &amp; Subs, Mac knows he's the only man who can track the killer. He's especially offended by the killer's extreme violation of victims' trust, since people in the scene generally don't take their play outside of the fetish clubs unless they've established trust. <br /><br />On Mac's first night at The Zone, he meets Mistress Violet who happens to be on her first unsupervised night (she's just completed shadowing and learning from The Zone's best Master, Tyler). Although a sub, Mac is a wild one to be tamed, and he's been manipulating his Mistresses for years! He says he doesn't need a safe word, but that's because Mac has charmed his way out of truly submitting. "Mistresses aren't made. They're Born." Violet may be petite compared to Mac, but she's the real deal and completely up for the challenge. Their journey is an emotional one, and the focus of the book. I didn't feel Mac conducted much investigating. Sure, he was occasionally at some crime scenes and staying up late trying to track the killer. And the story makes reference to Mac digging patrons of The Zone for information when Violet isn't around. But this is all about Mac and Violet's journey, and her breaking down his emotional layers. Violet wants it all - a man she can take home, live with and love - marriage, children...and she wants her man to completely trust her, reveal his inner thoughts, and completely let go to her control. <br /><br />The BDSM aspects: Violet did put Mac through some extreme situations, but she was also very nurturing and would definitely let Mac take control when they needed it. Violet wanted to quickly cut through Mac's bullshit, so these were his instructions if he wanted a 2nd night in her equine-themed playroom (with an optional voyeur panel for The Zone's members' enjoyment): <br /><br />"I'll come back here tomorrow between nine and eleven. If you want me, you'll be in this room, stripped. Nothing on. You put on one of the c**k harnesses, tether yourself to that ring in the floor, the minimum of amount of slack necessary between it and your c**k, your knees spread as wide as you can get them, your hands laced on the back of your head." Mac has to stay in this position until Violet decided to come down to him. Initially, she needs to break down his barriers, but I do feel things lightened up with him. <br /><br />The more violent, uncomfortable aspects of the BDSM scene did happen, but not at Violet's hand. I don't want to say anything more, for fear of spoiling it. Was Natural Law able to knock down my top 5 erotic romances reads from their podium? No, but this was nevertheless sophisticated, impressive erotic suspense. I own the next 2 books in this series, which are actually the story of one hero &amp; heroine, but told through 2 books that must be read together: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/177518.Ice_Queen" title="Ice Queen by Joey W. Hill" rel="nofollow noopener">Ice Queen</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1285705.Nature_of_Desire_Mirror_of_My_Soul" title="Nature of Desire Mirror of My Soul by Joey W. Hill" rel="nofollow noopener">Nature of Desire: Mirror of My Soul</a>. I hear they are amazing and I'm looking forward to reading them shortly :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="2909041430596049587" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</blockquote><br><br><br>Let me just preface this review by saying that our male sub, Mac, is by no means a pussy hero. He is strong, alpha, protective, is a homicide detective by day and is just an all-round hotty. Perfect book boyfriend material. So I was so intrigued to find out how that would translate when he hit the D/s scene. And, I don't know how accurate a representation this is, but hell, it totally worked for me. <br><br>I really didn't expect to find a male sub hot. But oh my God, some of these scenes were <i>so</i> sexy!!<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You’ll need to take it easy on him, Tyler. He comes off tough as nails, but if you find the way in, he can be hurt.<br><br>We all can, love. We all can.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>This is a mature erotic romance. Mac is in his forties and I think Violet is in her thirties. There's the addition of a murder investigation, too, so it isn't simply a BDSM porno, but there is a <i>lot</i> of sex in <i>Natural Law</i>. There are some really uncomfortable situations that were a little like car crashes. I was cringing and reading though my hands covering my eyes, but I just couldn't look away. And there are some scenes that had me threatening to burn a hole through my bed sheets they were so hot. <br><br>I loved that Mac was so resistant against his natural instincts. It's like the author is anticipating the judgement and pre-conceived ideas that a reader might have when they open this book. Mac's naturally submissive, enjoys giving himself over to his Mistress, but everything in him, every alpha male bone in his body, every part of him that wants to confirm to what society expects of a 'real man', rebels against his submissive nature. And it's super juicy watching Violet break down his defences and getting him to admit who he really is inside.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“This man was big. Over six feet, the broadness in his shoulders was enough to accelerate her heart rate. He was pure male animal. No matter what soap, deodorant or cologne he used, he wouldn’t be able to obliterate the scent. He was powerful, a predator, but what made him absolutely irresistible to her, overriding her common sense, was that he was a sexual submissive. An alpha wolf who chose the role of beta in the bedroom, but only for the right woman.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>I really enjoyed Violet's character. She's pint-sized, and feisty, and strong, and independent. And she falls hook, line and sinker for Mac. The emotional connection between these two fascinated me. There is so much sex in this book that you'd think there wouldn't be page space for the emotional stuff, too. But there totally is. And I think the sexual encounters, the trust that they have to have for one another, totally compounds that and strengthens everything the feel for one another outside of the bedroom/playroom/dungeon.<br><br>I'd really highly recommend this book for any BDSM romance lovers or for anyone, curious, as I was, to read about a <i>male</i> sub, for a change.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1389786435i/8054383._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>My blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://smittensbookblog.wordpress.com/">http://smittensbookblog.wordpress.com/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="18041954137820878258" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1184702140" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1184702140" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1184702140?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heidi Belleau" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heidi Belleau" href="/user/show/5891947-heidi-belleau">Heidi Belleau</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18632594-natural-law">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1184702140" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1228336341517679236">ARGH!<br/><br/>Reasons I hated this book:<br/>- the cliche setup. which probably wasn't cliche back when it was written (way back in 2004 which is like a million years ago when dinosaurs still roamed the earth in ebook years), but nowadays it's like OH LORD UNDERCOVER COP IN AN EXCLUSIVE BDSM CLUB FULL OF BEAUTIFUL RICH BDSM PEOPLE SOLVING BDSM MURDERS!<br/>- head hopping. not only did the POV switch between the two mains from paragraph to paragraph without warning or fanfare, but we occasionally got to pop into ot</span>
  <span id="freeText1228336341517679236" style="display:none">ARGH!<br /><br />Reasons I hated this book:<br />- the cliche setup. which probably wasn't cliche back when it was written (way back in 2004 which is like a million years ago when dinosaurs still roamed the earth in ebook years), but nowadays it's like OH LORD UNDERCOVER COP IN AN EXCLUSIVE BDSM CLUB FULL OF BEAUTIFUL RICH BDSM PEOPLE SOLVING BDSM MURDERS!<br />- head hopping. not only did the POV switch between the two mains from paragraph to paragraph without warning or fanfare, but we occasionally got to pop into other (seriously secondary) characters' heads as well. I found this super jarring. I dunno if it was supposed to be omniscient or what, but I definitely much prefer a close limited third POV, and if you do too, now you know.<br />- constant harping on about how the lead is an Alpha Alpha Alpha. this isn't a trope I like AT ALL and when it's drilled in endlessly the way it was here, it just makes me roll my eyes. which I did . . . a lot. not exactly the response you're looking for in an erotic thriller.<br />- the use of the term "murderess", completely straight faced, like this is some victorian penny dreadful instead of a modern novel. it was just . . . weird. gendering "murderer" that way is just so cheezy and lurid and I couldn't take seriously the concept that an officer of the law would ever use it<br />- the sex, despite being in a book of femdom/malesub, eventually denegrating into ME MAN YOU WOMAN ME TAKE YOU I AM ALPHA MALE bullshit that had me yawning. why establish such a sexy, uncliche dynamic . . . and then just bait and switch me with the same shitty e-rom tropes of a million other bdsm novels (which I normally DO NOT read? for a reason!) I liked a powerful masculine man (although gag me at calling him ~alpha~) being a sexual submissive. it's what drew me into the novel, but then partway through the story that just . . . stopped. it was like two different novels pasted together. one with a guy getting his ass plugged while a woman taunted and teased him and walked away . . . and the other him ~taking her like an animal~ etc etc etc <br />- the bdsm 101 infodumping. not only did it feel like a constant lecture on bdsm as if it was some kind of alien orientation outside of average human understanding, but sometimes it felt . . . downright condescending and dismissive of ~Vanilla~ relationships and people? Vanilla sex isn't as intense, Vanilla relationships aren't as dedicated, Vanilla people just don't "get it" and are closed minded and shitty. at the beginning I just skimmed because I'm no BDSM newcomer and found the info boring and unnecessary to the story, but as it wore on it started to remind me of encounters with the worst kind of straight kinksters. no thanks on that one. once again, all this might be a product of its times. BDSM fiction is barely outside of the mainstream anymore (and some subgenres/tropes have gone COMPLETELY mainstream) whereas this book may have had more obstacles to overcome for understanding.<br />- the identity of the "murderess" <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ who was one of the two only black women of the book. the other, her twin sister, was an incestuous abuser who also attempted murder at one point. left a really bad taste in my mouth <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />- the mystery in general was just sort of meh. there was no setup where potential suspects were introduced and then slowly ruled out. instead, there was a paragraph that brought up a couple potentials, and then immediately ruled them out, and then a paragraph later the true murderer revealed herself. we didn't see the investigation, any of the detective work. this book really could have just been about the whole Alpha Submissive and his inward struggle and left the whole murder mystery conceit behind. if you're going to write a mystery, then write it, I guess? it felt like a whole lot of window dressing.<br />- at one point our alpha sub declares he doesn't use or need safewords and his Dom doesn't immediately tell him to shape up or ship out. she does give him a safe word (which he immediately swears he'll never use), but I just wasn't comfortable with her going ahead with him knowing that was his intention. I like my consensual books consensual.<br />- hero had a moustache, yuck.<br /><br />Reasons I loved this book:<br />- male sub with chest hair<br />- reluctant assplay :P~~~~~~ (at first, see above)<br /><br />I'm so desperate for a book about a male submissive and a female dominant that I read through this despite my constant irritation at multiple tropes that really are Not For Me. the sex sure was hot in the beginning, but man, it just makes me wish I could find and read a femdom book that's more in line with my reading tastes. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1228336341517679236" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12699483094601880165">I really didn't know if I would like this book. I am not into female Doms. Plus, any BDSM books I read are not hardcore...I like them milder. I am not one to like to cringe when I read about hurtful foreplay between two (or more) characters, and I certainly don't like it when the sub is humiliated.   <span id="freeText12699483094601880165" style="display:none">I really didn't know if I would like this book. I am not into female Doms. Plus, any BDSM books I read are not hardcore...I like them milder. I am not one to like to cringe when I read about hurtful foreplay between two (or more) characters, and I certainly don't like it when the sub is humiliated. That just doesn't do it for me. <br />Having said that, I really did like this book. It is a little strong in areas of their "play", but I thought the love story between the two characters were well thought out. I could definately see how they grew to love and trust one another. I was surprised about that. I don't know if I will continue to read any Female Dom stories, (I like my men in charge...although the hero in this story is very alpha) but I am glad I gave this one a shot. <br />If you are offended by strong language, M/M/F interaction, BDSM scenerios...then this book is DEFINATELY not for you.<br /></span>

  <span id="freeText7564213630793245985" style="display:none">This was recommended to me a while back and I've finally got around to reading it. I always go into BDSM books a little worried because the lifestyle can require sharing and multiple partners.<br /><br />This was not a big issue for me in this story. The situations with multiple participants were still very much focussed on the main couples relationship so did not set off my cheating alarm.<br /><br />The story itself was billed as a bit of a thriller and about half way in I was wondering what happened because it was all about Mackenzie and Violet. But it did pick up then with some edge of the seat stuff happening in the latter part of the book.<br /><br />So overall this book was really about the developing relationship of Mac and Violet as they develop a Domme/Sub thing. It was unusual for me to see a female Domme and male Sub as I haven't read many of this sub-genre. It wasn't totally new though so I was able to concentrate on the story which was engrossing. I really liked Mac and Violet and the romance storyline.<br /><br />It was very explicit at times and the BDSM stuff was explained well without being overly intrusive.</span>

<div id="review_85310172" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/85310172" />
    <a title="Davina D." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2272230-davina-d"><img alt="Davina D." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1270369919p2/2272230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/85310172?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Davina D." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Davina D." href="/user/show/2272230-davina-d">Davina D.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2272230-davina-d?shelf=erotic-romance-with-plot">erotic-romance-with-plot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2272230-davina-d?shelf=2010-reads">2010-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2272230-davina-d?shelf=good-reads">good-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2272230-davina-d?shelf=bdsm-hardcore">bdsm-hardcore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2272230-davina-d?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2272230-davina-d?shelf=beta-heroes">beta-heroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2272230-davina-d?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2272230-davina-d?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2272230-davina-d?shelf=fake-alpha-heroes">fake-alpha-heroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2272230-davina-d?shelf=light-menage-sexual-interaction">light-menage-sexual-interaction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer85310172" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15054037058139672">Well, I'll never look at a big, burly guy the same way again. That's for sure! :)<br/><br/>This is not my first foray into the world of BDSM, but this book clearly drew the line between the tamer depictions of the D/s lifestyle I've read in books and what I imagine the real thing to be. On occasion I do like to spice up my reading with material containing alternative sexual activities and boy did I get what I was looking for here! Now, I'm no fairy. I've certainly been around the block a couple of times i</span>
  <span id="freeText15054037058139672" style="display:none">Well, I'll never look at a big, burly guy the same way again. That's for sure! :)<br /><br />This is not my first foray into the world of BDSM, but this book clearly drew the line between the tamer depictions of the D/s lifestyle I've read in books and what I imagine the real thing to be. On occasion I do like to spice up my reading with material containing alternative sexual activities and boy did I get what I was looking for here! Now, I'm no fairy. I've certainly been around the block a couple of times in my heyday, but this novel had me squirming in equal amounts of delight and discomfiture. Having read Holding the Cards, Book 1 of Hill's Nature of Desire series, before this, I ought not to have been shocked, but I was <i>shocked</i>, and like its predecessor Natural Law rattled the cage of my comfort zone on more than one occasion. <br /><br />Nevertheless, once the more hardcore stuff had been related this was quite an enjoyable read and a fairly well written novel. Hill has a very vivid way with words. Sometimes too vivid when you consider the story's context. :)<br /><br />What I like about Hill's work is that she's able to take an easily misrepresented and misinterpreted lifestyle such as D/s and infuse it with so much depth and emotion that even the vanilla-est of readers can come to appreciate her characters and the choices they make.<br /><br />That said, what ultimately robbed this book of an additional 1,5 stars for me is Hill's execution. And this very much has to do with the more technical side of writing. It tried to be too many things at once. First it started off with a very strong, hardcore D/s angle then that just sort of tapered off into the more "mundane" aspects of the story. In other words it jumped from a story about D/s with very strong romantic undertones to a more standard romance, if you will. <br /><br />It was as though Hill suddenly remembered that 1) she had to go back and develop the murder plot line she had previously introduced and 2) slow down with the hardcore stuff so as not to scare off readers. Of course its unrealistic, considering her general audience ("vanilla" romance readers and hardcore erotica fans alike), to expect that the more explicit D/s play could have proceeded throughout the book at the same high octane level as in the first quarter of the novel (and in fact I'm personally glad it didn't!), but there wasn't a very neat transition from one aspect of the story to the next in my opinion. <br /><br />Also Mac the hero, although I have no complaints about him, is not really the type of hero I tend to go for. I prefer my heroes alpha all the way, both in and out of the bedroom; and while Violet was likeable enough, I'm not really into female Doms. I just think he came off a little too fantastic--I prefer a guy a bit more rough around the edges, especially one who's a cop. What Hill's narrative showed me was that he was indeed a very beta hero. Nothing wrong with that of course -- I think under the skill of a good author the beta hero makes one of the best romance heroes around. That said, what Hill showed me and what she told me were two different characters.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15054037058139672" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_728134484" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/728134484" />
    <a title="Vanessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12059859-vanessa"><img alt="Vanessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576765878p2/12059859.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/728134484?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vanessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vanessa" href="/user/show/12059859-vanessa">Vanessa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/18428739-natural-law">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12059859-vanessa?shelf=alpha-assholes-i-love">alpha-assholes-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12059859-vanessa?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12059859-vanessa?shelf=bdsm">bdsm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12059859-vanessa?shelf=mental-issues">mental-issues</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer728134484" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4221351046562732930">I loved this book... I really did!! Wow, what a deliciously unexpected surprise!!!<br/><br/>Natural Law by Joey W. Hill is perhaps one of the best BDSM/romance books I've ever read. I've been burned with this genre so many times, that I've retreated...but I have missed the edge of a good BDSM erotica read. Sadly, I have found that too many books in this genre offer to be one thing, but in actuality, what you get is a bad, sleazy porn with little to no plot, character development, or story....just filler t</span>
  <span id="freeText4221351046562732930" style="display:none">I loved this book... I really did!! Wow, what a deliciously unexpected surprise!!!<br /><br />Natural Law by Joey W. Hill is perhaps one of the best BDSM/romance books I've ever read. I've been burned with this genre so many times, that I've retreated...but I have missed the edge of a good BDSM erotica read. Sadly, I have found that too many books in this genre offer to be one thing, but in actuality, what you get is a bad, sleazy porn with little to no plot, character development, or story....just filler that rolls between sex scene to sex scene. <br /><br />This book was highly recommended by one of my fave bloggers who never does me wrong, so right away, I knew I had to give it a shot....and DAMN, am I glad I did!!! Great characters, great premise, unique, engrossing plot, wonderful dialogue, heart pumping suspense, and yes, some very hot sex. But the best thing of all is that underneath all of that, there is a layer of incredible tenderness, sweetness, and love between these two characters, desperately seeking a connection and understanding. <br /><br />Even if you think that BDSM is not for you, I would still urge you to give this one a try. The parts of BDSM that I really have a problem with are the humiliation and demoralizing acts....there is little to none of this here. What little there is, is more from the secondary characters, and within the general environment, not among the main characters. Seriously, this is not a smutty book at all. More about sensuality rather than hard core sex and dominant sexual acts. There was really only one scene that pushed my comfort level but it was more a feeling of shock rather than disgust.<br /><br />Violet is a Domme at a high level, descrete BDSM club. She is a domme to her core. When she meets Mackenzie, she is instantly mesmerized. He is 6 feet of gorgeous man and she cannot wait to sink her teeth in. She immediately senses that he is a sexual submissive...but, emphasis on the "sexual." This man does not have a submissive hair on his body in any of the other parts of his life. He is a high profile homicide detective and 100% alpha bad ass! <br /><br />When the latest murderer at large is targeting male sexual submissives like himself, things become personal for Mackenzie. While undercover, Mackenzie meets Violet, a young, beautiful Domme that calls to him on his every primal level. <br /><br />What starts as a cover for Mackenzie and an itch to be scratched for Violet, quickly escalates into something neither of them expected to find. And OMG, their reaction to each other is off the charts!!! Talk about pulling (more like yanking) at the heart stings!!! As Violet slowly strips him of his defensive armour, Mackenzie finally starts truly embracing his submissive proclivities, drawing pleasure, both physical as well as emotional, from exposing his vulnerabilities to his Mistress and surrendering all control. <br /><br />I won't say any more except that the story takes off from there. This book had everything...steam, romance, passion, psychological thriller, action, suspense.....my heart was pounding the whole time!!<br /><br />The whole story with the murder case is not sorta going on in the background...it is a very palpable, real part of the story line that will keep you guessing the whole book....and I totally did not see the truth coming!!!<br /><br />I really have to applaud Ms. Hill. The plot is so intricately thought out...the ins and outs of it...it is obvious that she is a seasoned writing veteran! <br /><br />Finally, the story line also goes on to truly define the lifestyle that is a part of our main characters...who they really are, in a very realistic way. They have to struggle with acceptance and against what society deems them...freaks, sexual deviants....this all comes full circle for these characters in a beautiful, honest and powerful way. Perfection!!!<br /><br />A very HEA and epilogue is involved! I immediately downloaded the next two books in this series as soon as I was done! Can't wait to read Tyler and Mistress Marguerite next!!! A refreshing, bad-ass, edgy, romantic, beautiful read that you do not want to miss!!!<br /><br /><b> 5/5 SEXY HEART-FELT DOMINATING STARS!!! </b><br /><br /><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/103359.Joey_W__Hill" title="Joey W. Hill" rel="nofollow noopener">Joey W. Hill</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4221351046562732930" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/87446618?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/3071767-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer87446618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1721998409411189023">Being one of TPD’s premiere homicide detectives Mackenzie “Mac” Nighthorse never thought he would find himself embroiled in a case that would force him to confess his own sexual fetish to his boss. Yet now he is stunned to find himself undercover at one of the most select D/s clubs Tampa has, The Zone, seeking the serial killer of some of its male submissives. <br/><br/>Violet Siemanski, one of The Zones newest female Dominants, is stunned when one of the sexiest male submissives she has ever seen crosses</span>
  <span id="freeText1721998409411189023" style="display:none">Being one of TPD’s premiere homicide detectives Mackenzie “Mac” Nighthorse never thought he would find himself embroiled in a case that would force him to confess his own sexual fetish to his boss. Yet now he is stunned to find himself undercover at one of the most select D/s clubs Tampa has, The Zone, seeking the serial killer of some of its male submissives. <br /><br />Violet Siemanski, one of The Zones newest female Dominants, is stunned when one of the sexiest male submissives she has ever seen crosses her path on her first solo night out. She is quick to make her move and capture the attention of this six-foot, broad shouldered sub. Yet she is staggered when Mac rebuffs her, she feels the connection between them that could lead them both to Nirvana. <br /><br />Mac is astonished to feel that same connection, but he is at The Zone on a mission to stop a killer not to find the mistress of his dreams. Never does he imagine that Violet will lead him into a journey of enlightenment that will set his true submissive side loose. But will Mac and Violet reach Nirvana before Mac becomes the next sub on the killers list? That is the true issue.<br /><br />I was leery to invest my time into reading a book about a male submissive. I being a woman, and not a sexually Dominate one; usually find myself desiring to read stories about Alpha males that lovingly subjugate the women in their lives, meaning I like books where the man is the Dom and the woman is the sub. But Natural Law is a story unlike any that I have ever read before. Don’t get me wrong the BDSM elements in this story are just phenomenal; in fact they are some of the most unsurpassed sex scenes I have ever read. But this story is so much more then BDSM, it is a story of a spiritual awakening and understanding between two powerful Alpha souls. It just turns out that the woman is the sexual dominant and the man is the sexual submissive. Your probably thinking, come on how absorbing can this book be? Well let me tell you it is TOTALLY. I had to step away from it many times to catch my own bearings, but I was drawn back to it before my ebook reader had time to cool off. If you have ever read one of Joey W. Hill’s books you probably know she is a writer that can craft a truly enthralling story but Natural Law goes well beyond enthralling, in fact it actually enters the realm of obsessive. The sex is explosive, the love story is riveting and that doesn’t even include the murder mystery, which is spectacular, I was truly shocked at the identity of the killer. I never saw it coming. LOL!!!!<br /><br />Ms. Hill has crafted a story that is so well written that the characters, main and minor, demand your attention and respect. They literally came to life for me. I found Natural Law to be so intriguing that I wanted to enter this world and find out as much as I could. I know it is only a story, but it made me think so much that I did some researching of my own into the D/s world and have joined a Yahoo Group wanting to understand this fetish more. I will be recommending this book to anyone and everyone who comes across my path looking for a good book to spend some time with. Let me just say that Natural Law is so far beyond the norm for an erotica book that if there were a Pulitzer for erotica I would ask for it to be passed this way. I think we have a winner here. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1721998409411189023" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11029322745936919558"><b>REVIEW OF AUDIOBOOK; OCTOBER 16, 2013: <br/>ONE STAR:(<br/>Narrator: Maxine Mitchell :(</b><br/><br/>This is a review only of the audio version. For the story, read my review below from 2006.<br/><br/>I wasn't going to buy this because 1) there were no sample audios available, 2) the only samples were of Mitchell narrating other books and omigod, she was awful.<br/><br/>I ended up buying because 1) it was only $3.95 and 2) the sample for this book was finally available and Mitchell's voice came off much better here than the in other books</span>
  <span id="freeText11029322745936919558" style="display:none"><b>REVIEW OF AUDIOBOOK; OCTOBER 16, 2013: <br />ONE STAR:(<br />Narrator: Maxine Mitchell :(</b><br /><br />This is a review only of the audio version. For the story, read my review below from 2006.<br /><br />I wasn't going to buy this because 1) there were no sample audios available, 2) the only samples were of Mitchell narrating other books and omigod, she was awful.<br /><br />I ended up buying because 1) it was only $3.95 and 2) the sample for this book was finally available and Mitchell's voice came off much better here than the in other books.<br /><br />I ended up asking for a refund because once again, the sample is inadequate when gauging whether a narrator suits me. All I can tell from the sample is whether I like the sound of the voice but to know whether he/she is a good narrator (IMO) I need at least a chapter.<br /><br />For Mitchell, I could barely tolerate a whole chapter but I forced myself to get through 3 chapters after which I took pity upon myself. While Mitchell's voice wasn't as tinny and whiny as the samples I'd heard, listening to her for a whole chapter left me feeling weirdly seasick. Yep. Seasick, because Mitchell does this rolling pitch with her words, stressing and lifting one syllable over another. Right through the chapter, to another. If I'd finished the book, I'm sure I'd have thrown up.<br /><br />I asked for a refund. Don't believe Audible when it says on their website you can return a book online just by clicking the 'eligible' button. That doesn't happen. Once they process a return, your book is removed from your library so if it's still there then your return hasn't been processed. I had returns requested months or weeks ago that were never processed and only found out when I contacted them to inquire why the 'eligible' button was still there.<br /><br /><br />-----------------------------------------------------------------------<br /><br />Finally. An erotic suspense that has all three elements I want: erotic sex, suspense and romance.<br /><br />One of my keepers and worth a re-read.<br /><br />I didn't know much about the BDSM lifestyle before I read Joey Hill and though more informed these days, it's still not a turn-on for me so when I read that Mac is a submissive, it took me awhile before I decided to buy this book. BDSM as well as my hero a submissive? With Morgan Hawke still fresh in my mind, I wondered if I was going to get my hero pissed on by the heroine.<br /><br />I needn't have worried. Joey Hill writes in a particular way that's reminiscent of a serious fiction. I don't know if her other titles are the same but I bought Ice Queen and took a peek and the writing style and language is the same. Anyway, there're no golden showers in Natural Law if I recall correctly but plenty of everything else.<br /><br />Mac is also not the kind of submissive male I'm thinking of. He's still alpha, confident and in control. Makes you curious, doesn't it, how someone like him is a sexual submissive.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1686537848915342103"><br/><br/>I was going to add Natural Law to my "guilty pleasure" shelf, but stopped just as I was about to click beside it.<br/><br/>See, because it'd be so easy to do that and simply underestimate the importance of this story, cataloging it along with well-written and sex-filled books that, although highly entertaining, didn't left anything behind them that isn't a dreamy smirk and a heartfelt nod of my head.<br/><br/>No, Natural Law goes directly into my "favorite" shelf, as well as in a bunch of other well-deserved sexy a</span>
  <span id="freeText1686537848915342103" style="display:none"><br /><br />I was going to add Natural Law to my "guilty pleasure" shelf, but stopped just as I was about to click beside it.<br /><br />See, because it'd be so easy to do that and simply underestimate the importance of this story, cataloging it along with well-written and sex-filled books that, although highly entertaining, didn't left anything behind them that isn't a dreamy smirk and a heartfelt nod of my head.<br /><br />No, Natural Law goes directly into my "favorite" shelf, as well as in a bunch of other well-deserved sexy and mind-blowing-expressing shelves.<br /><br />I knew I was in for a life-altering experience as a reader when I read the book's plot. I'd never heard of a BDSM book where the male MC was your "average" alpha guy in his public life and a submissive in his private - a sub struggling with his own needs and desires. I could've given it a four-star rating for that reason alone. <br /><br />But the female MC being a Dominatrix was what really won me over.<br />It doesn't happen often to find a D/s relationship where the Dom is actually a woman. And what woman Violet is.<br /><br />Described as "petite" and "fair-skinned" so much to resemble a fairy, she's relatively new to the BDSM scene, but "was born a mistress".<br />That's one of the things that I liked the most about this book. The main characters' unapologetic view and approach to their own sexuality.<br />There's nothing to feel ashamed about or hide - at least not from themselves - in their lives. <br />That was refreshing and added so much more sensuality to the story.<br /><br />And Mac, the hero. A man whose body screamed "raw masculinity" but who was actually a sub terrified of relinquishing control. <br /><br />I've read a lot of different BDSM books, but I have to admit that I was really able to better understand the people involved in it and their psychology only with Natural Law. This is a whole new level of characterization, of sex-writing and of love-blossoming.<br /><br />The sex reached levels of head-spinning excitement. I rarely get embarrassed or shocked anymore, but Natural Law shocked me for all the good reasons.<br /><br />It was necessary for the reader to realize how powerful the connection between a Dom and her sub is. <br /><br />I loved everything about this story and I need to stop rambling now.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer320092401" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6039008002873249843">A one-star review of <i>Fifty Shades of Grey</i> introduced me to Joey Hill, and a flurry of generally positive reviews for Ms Hill’s forays into BDSM convinced me to give her a try. My three-star rating is for her competence with language and story, despite such vulgarisms as “the long length of him,” “gnoche,” (a phonetic rendering of ganache, which she clearly didn’t stop to look up in a dictionary); and “dominatrixes.” Though many romance novelists were capable of faultless grammar and impressively</span>
  <span id="freeText6039008002873249843" style="display:none">A one-star review of <i>Fifty Shades of Grey</i> introduced me to Joey Hill, and a flurry of generally positive reviews for Ms Hill’s forays into BDSM convinced me to give her a try. My three-star rating is for her competence with language and story, despite such vulgarisms as “the long length of him,” “gnoche,” (a phonetic rendering of ganache, which she clearly didn’t stop to look up in a dictionary); and “dominatrixes.” Though many romance novelists were capable of faultless grammar and impressively rich prose during the 60s, 70s, and 80s, Hill is a better prose stylist, overall, than most of the people writing in this genre today, a fact which undeniably places her above a lot of romantic shlock glutting the market; but, alas, this is just romantic shlock, after all. <br /><br />This observation may be less idiosyncratic than it may seem on the surface, but, for me, the cardinal difference between romance fiction and Romantic literature is that the latter is generally tragic, or involves a healthy dose of loss, depletion, inanition, and poetic mourning. <i>Natural Law</i> is, all said and done, a ridiculously happy book; and that, to me, is what fails to elevate it far enough above the pedestrian, despite its generally well-written BDSM elements. <br /><br />At the end of the whole thing, these two are madly in love with each other, and all irony, paradox, and cynicism have fled—leaving me bored and impatient for something edgy. I went in expecting BDSM Noir and I got spicy Harlequin. The murder mystery which frames the novel—and runs a secret thread behind its dirty colors to hang it on the generic wall—is, to put it mildly, as lame as the lamest Nancy Drew mystery. And without Nancy’s lovely pumps, pearls, and swing skirts to excuse the kind of plotting that would make Dame Agatha Christie blush. So that leaves you with a pair of lovebirds who like to play with whips and strap-ons, but who are, at the end of the day, as far from truly liberal—in their configuration of chivalry and monogamy—as the blandest Hallmark wedding card. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6039008002873249843" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1293979687" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1293979687" />
    <a title="Heather / Obsessed With Myshelf" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36526873-heather-obsessed-with-myshelf"><img alt="Heather / Obsessed With Myshelf" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424495008p2/36526873.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1293979687?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather / Obsessed With Myshelf" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather / Obsessed With Myshelf" href="/user/show/36526873-heather-obsessed-with-myshelf">Heather / Obsessed With Myshelf</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1293979687" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5929826146964396878">A male alpha homicide detective submissive?! I have now read it all. This is a suspenseful BDSM romance that had my eyes lowered to the page, begging for release. Violet and Mac are dynamic together – the give and take of their relationship is so balanced and yet utterly complex. This pushed me out if my comfort zone in a good way.<br/><br/>I can’t believe that this was first published in 2004. Joey was blazing a path that has exploded into the romance that we know and love today – SO THANK YOU. thankyout</span>
  <span id="freeText5929826146964396878" style="display:none">A male alpha homicide detective submissive?! I have now read it all. This is a suspenseful BDSM romance that had my eyes lowered to the page, begging for release. Violet and Mac are dynamic together – the give and take of their relationship is so balanced and yet utterly complex. This pushed me out if my comfort zone in a good way.<br /><br />I can’t believe that this was first published in 2004. Joey was blazing a path that has exploded into the romance that we know and love today – SO THANK YOU. thankyouthankyou. Natural Law is well written and pulls you into the BDSM world. Before I knew it, I was bolted to the pages and hanging on for dear life.<br /><br />Someone is killing sexual submissive men – and the police believe it’s a Mistress. These are smart men who haven’t published their sexual preferences, which makes finding the killer harder than the police initially think.<br /><br />Mac is a cop. He’s big, he’s strong, he’s driven &amp; he’s also a sexual submissive. He doesn’t have a safeword, but that’s because he has ridiculous charm that he manages to use to top from the bottom. But when he meets Violet at The Zone while he’s working undercover, she’s sees right through his bullshit. As Violet pushes past the barriers Mac has built around his heart, they soon realize that their relationship is turning into far more than either of them realized.<br /><br />I’m not usually comfortable with group sex acts, but somehow Joey takes what could be an extremely uncomfortable scene and makes you feel the connection between the two main characters, pushing everyone else to the side. I loved Violet’s strength and dominance. I also loved that she was all woman – she isn’t overly aggressive or mean – and she uses her position over Mac in a completely believable way.<br /><br />This book blew my mind. GREATread.<br /><br />This review looks prettier on my blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://obsessedwithmyshelf.com/2015/07/04/review-natural-law-by-joey-w-hill/">http://obsessedwithmyshelf.com/2015/0...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5929826146964396878" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WySi+FhZMUEe+Q2yQerYz5RwEHIkgyhY6P6GKgNXxQ/+B/Owuwu1ImWF5jy1RPPBFLlWF9nTNw8MAMtO/9YQwg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {

    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }
